And be it enacted by the authority aforesaid, That from and after the said twenty-fourth day of June* one thousand seven hundred and seventy-two, no tea, exceeding the quantity of six pounds weight, shall be removed or carried from any part of this kingdom by land or by water without a permit or certificate, signed by one or more of the officers for the inland duties on tea, signifying and certifying the names and places of abode of the buyer and feller, and expressing the quantity and quality of the tea* that is to say, if the tea so to be removed or carried is bohea, oongo, fouchong, or pekoe tea, then to express in the permit or certificate that the same is black tea; and if the tea so to be removed and carried is neither bohea, Congo, foueboag, or pekoe tea, then to express in the permit or certificate that the same is Grass tea, and also certifying that the inland duties chargeable upon tea have been duly paid and satisfied, upon pan of forfeiting the tea which is lo found removing or carrying from one place to another without such permit or certificate, expressing the quality as abovesaid, together with the package in which the same shall be contained, which permit or certificate shall be left with the officer of the division to which the same shall be carried, to prevent the seizure thereof, in which permit or certificate the officer who grants the same shall express and limit the time for which the lame shall continue in force.

CAP. LXL'

An act to regulate the makings keeping y and carriage of gunpowder, within Great Britain and to repeal the laws hen-t of ore made for any of those purposes.

WHEREAS the manufacture of gunpowder within Grez Britain, though necessary to he encouraged in resptft of i-. value of gunpowder, as an article of defence and commerce, jet oe?h to be regulated by law, in order to prevent the great mischiefs may arise from explofons occafmed by the improper conjiruftiou &i nfe of the mills, engines, and buildings, employed in the making of gr*-powdery and for keeping and carrying gunpowder in too great tities, or in an improper manner: and whereas the act pqffcd in ? lajf J'ejfton of parliament, intituled An act for reducing into one» of parliament the several laws relating to the keeping and arriage of gunpowder, and for more effectually preventing mli chiefs, by keeping or carrying gunpowder in too great quarni-ties, contains no provision for regulating the making of gttnpewdr, and is in other respects defeftivey on which account it may be estez: -nient to repeal the said act, andy in the room thereof \ to have a err law for regulating, as well the making as the keeping and carriage d gunpowder \ be it therefore enacted by the King's most excelfet majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the lords spiritts1 and temporal, and commons, in this present parliament atffcm-bled, and by the authority of the same, That no person or persons shall use, or cause to be used any mill or mills, or other engine or engines, for the making of gunpowder, or ir> any ma-ner manufacture gunpowder in any place or places within Grai Britain, except in mills and other places where the mranufaftare of gunpowder shall be actually carrying on at the time of the commencement of this act, or where it shall afterwards becom: lawful to carry on such manufacture, by obtaining a licence for that purpose, under the provisions herein-after contained, upen pain of forfeiting all gunpowder manufactured contrary to the aforesaid provision, and also two shillings for every pound of such gunpowder.

II. And be it further enacted by the authority aforesaid, That no person or persons whatsoever shall, for the making of gunpowder, employ, work, or use, any mill or engine, worked with a pestle or pestles, and commonly called a Pejlle Milly upon pain of forfeiting all gunpowder manufactured therein, and also two shillings for every pound of such gunpowder.

III. And be it further enacted by the authority aforesaid, That no person or persons whatsoever shall, in or with any mill or engine used for the making of gunpowder, make or cause to be made, at any one time under any single pair of mill stones, any quantity of gunpowder, or materials to be made into gunpowder, exceeding forty pounds, upon pain of forfeiting all gunpowder so made at one time, and exceeding the said quantity of forty pounds, and also two shillings for every pound of such gunpowder.

XIX. And be it further enacted by the authority aforesaid, That when any barge, boat, or vessel, having stale, condemned, or returned gunpowder on board, arrives at the wharf, key, or other place where the same is intended to be landed, no person or persons shall begin to unload, or shall bring down to such wharf, key, or other place, with intent to load in such vessel any other gunpowder, until the whole, or a part of such stale, condemned, or returned gunpowder, be first unloaded and carried away from such whan, key, or other place of landing; and after such unloading and carrying away of part of such gunpowder, no person or persons shall begin to load, or shall so bring down, with intent to load, any greater quantity of other gunpowder than the part unloaded and carried away, on pain of forfeiting all such gunpowder as shall be so brought down or loaded contrary to the aforesaid provision,

XXVIII. And be it further enacted, That all actions, suits, and prosecutions, to be commenced in England* against any person or persons, for any thing to be done in pursuance of this act, shall be laid and tried in the county or place where the fact was committed, and shall be commenced within six calendar months after the fast committed, and not otherwise.

XXIX. Provided always, and be it further enacted, That this act shall not extend, or be any ways construed to extend, to any mills or other buildings erested, or which may hereafter be erested, for the purpose of making gunpowder, in any lands belonging to his Majesty, his heirs or successors, or to the keep, ing of gunpowder at any storehouse or magazine belonging to his Majesty, his heirs or successors, or to hinder the trial ot gunpowder byhis Majesty's officers, as is usual, for the service of his Majesty, his heirs or successors, or to the keeping of'gun-power at the magazines now erected for that purpose of Bari-ing, Creekfmouib* in the county of Essex* and Erith Lruel* in the county of Kent* or to the keeping of gunpowder at the magazines or storehouses now erected near Liverpooli* in the county of Lancaster* or the city of Bristol* or to the carriage of gunpowder, to or from the King's magazines, under a special and express order of the King's board of ordnance; such order to contain the quantity of gunpowder so to be carried, and the time for which such order shall be in force*or to the carri^e of gunpowder with forces on their march, or with the militia, during their annual exercise; or which shall be font for the use of such forces or militia.

XXX. Provided also, and be it further ensured* That this present act shall not extend to hinder any person or perfoas from carrying or conveying an unlimited quantity of gunpowder, in such close-decked vessels, and manner as herein-before is directed, from any ships or vessels lying below Blackwall* to any of the magazines for gunpowder, so situate below Blatkwati, or from such magazines to any ships or vessels lying below Blod-tvally and going to any place beyond sea, or coastwise.

XXXI. And be it further enacted by the authority aforesaid, That this act shall commence, and begin to be in force, on the first day of July* one thousand seven hundred and seventy-two; and from and immediately after the commencement thereof, an act made in the last session of this present parliament, (intituled An act for reducing into one act of parliament the several laws relaxing to the keeping and carriage of gunpowder, and for the mart effectually preventing mischiefs, by keeping or carrying gunpowder in ta great quantities)* and all former Statutes, so far as they relate to the keeping and carriage of gunpowder, shall be, and the same are hereby repealed.

XVII. Provided also, That in case any such contributor or adventurer as aforesaid, who shall have advanced and paid down to such cashier or cashiers a proportion of his, her, or their consideration-money towards the said lottery, his, her, or their executors, administrators, successors, or assigns, do not advance and pay unto such cashier or cashiers the remaining part of his, her, or their consideration-money, so to be paid in full for such ticket or tickets on or before the times for paying thereof as aforesaid; and in such case no ticker or tickets shall be delivered out by the said cashier or carriers to such contributor or contributors, adventurer or adventurers, making such default; but the ticket and tickets which Should have been delivered to them respectively, had they paid the full money for the same, shall be returned and delivered to the said managers and directors by the said cashier or carfhiers, together with the other tickets (if any} in the outermost column of the book and hooks first herein mentioned and directed to be prepared, which shall not have been disposed of as aforesaid; CAP. LXV.

An act to extinguish the right of common upon an acre ef ground called White Lyon, (nr Hangman's Acre, in Saint George's Fields, in the county xf Surrey.

[Preamble.]

WHEREAS the prison called The House of Corre£scion, in

the borough of Southwark, in the county of Surrey, is too

finally unhealthy, inconvenient, and unfofcy and persons committed u

the/aid prison for felony cannot be kept separate from those committed

for fmatt mijaemeanors, which greatly tends to the ruin and entire

corruption of the latter: and whereas it has, upon inquiry, been found

absolutely necessary to rebuild the J'aid prison in a more convenient

situation: and whereas the county of Surrey is feijed or pojfejpd of

an acre of ground in Saint George's Fields, called White Lyon,

or Hangman's Acre, Jituate near the King's Bench prisony which

is a proper place for erecting the faii house of correction: and whereas

the justices of the peace, at the quarter session of the peace held for the

said county, on the fourteenth day of January, one thousand fevers

hundred and/eventy-two* did unanimously agree to build a new house of correction on the said ground: but as the owners of certain lands in Saint George's Fields have a right of common for their cattle, at

certain times of the year9 upon the said acre9 promijeuously with other

lands, f though stich right is of no real value with respect to the said

aerty) the building cannot be. ere fled unless such right be extinguijbedy

which cannot be done without the authority of parliament: may it

therefore please your Majesty that it may be enacted; and be it

ing hereof advice and consent of the lords spirrruai and temporal, and

mil right of commons, in this present parliament assembled, and by the au-

Acre shall all right of common, or common of pasture, in, over, and upon

cease, and be the said acre of land called White Lyon % or Hangman's Acrey shall

extinguiftud. cease, determine, and be for ever extinguished.

CAP. LXVIL

An act for incorporating the members of a society, commonly called The Marine Society, and their successors, to he defied as therein is mentioned, and for the better impowering and enabling them to carry on their charitable and useful designs.

WHEREAS, in June one thousand seven hundred and fifty- preamblei fix, a society was instituted under certain regulations for fitting and placing out men and boys to the sea service, and other charitable purposes> commonly called The Marine Society j which said society, during the late war with France and Spain, and at different times ftnee the conclusion thereof by the voluntary donations and subscriptions of charitable and welUdisposed 'persons (amongst other charities) cloathed and fitted out five thousand four hundred and fifty-one landmen, to serve as seamen on board his Majesty's ships; and also cloatked, fitted, and placed out as servants or apprentices to officers in the King's ships, and to the merchants service at Jea9 six thousand three hundred and six boys, who had no visible means of jup -party and who voluntarily offered themselves: and whereas experience bath Jbewn, that the JaidJociety bath been hitherto of considerable ufey end an advantage to the nation, and it is apprehended that the said society, if countenanced and supported by the laws of this realm, and established upon a respefiable and permanent foundation, and vcjhd % uith proper powers for enabling them to carry into execution their charitable designsy (that is to say,) the fitting out and apprenticing, or placing outy poor difireffed boys9 to and for the strvice of the royal navy, end to and for the service of other ships and vessels9 the property of and belonging tOysubjefis of the King oj Great Britain, would be of much more extensive uje, and a fill greater benefit and advantage to these kingdoms, as being a means of supplying his Majesty's ships9 in lime of war9 withfeomen properly bred up and qualified Jor that service, and contributing to the commercial inter ejls of the nation in time of peace \ and also by ajfijling the inward police thereof in providing for the idle, and consequently mofi dangerous members of society: but as it is apprehended that these salutary measures cannot be condufied with any degree of vigour, nor these useful ends attained in their full extenty without the aid and authority of parliament; may it therefore please your most excellent Majesty that it may be enacted; and be it enacted by the King's most excellent majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the lords spiritual and temporal, andcommons, in this present parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, That the right honourable Robert lord Romney baron of Romney9 the right honourable Robert lord Clive baron of Plaffey9 in the kingdom of Ireland, knight of the most honourable order of the bath, sir William Dolben baronet, fir George Pococie knight of the most honourable order of the bath,

CAP. LXXII.

An act for rendering the payment of the creditors of insolvent debtors more equal and expeditious, and fer regulating the diligence of the law by arrefiment and poindings and for extending the privilege of bills to promissory notes, and for limiting actions upon bills and promissory notes, in that part of Great Britain called Scotland.

WHEREAS by the laws now fubfifing in that part of Great Preamble, Britain called Scotland, the personal estates of such debtors as become insolvent are generally carried off by the diligences of arrefi-went and poindings executed by a few creditors, whoy from the near-nefs of their resideme toy and connexion with such debtors, get the ear lie ft notice of the insolvency, to the great prejudice of creditors more remote and unconnected, and to the disappointment of that equality which ought to take place in the distribution of the estates of insolvent debtors among their creditors: therefore, to remedy such injufiice and inequality in time coming, and to render the payment of the creditors of insolvent debtors more equal and expeditious, may it please your most excellent Majesty that it may be enacted; and be it enacted by the King's most excellent majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the lords spiritual and temporal, and commons, in this present parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, That when any debtor, in that part of Great Britain called Scotland, shall suffer a poinding on a horning, or on the^i, tors precept of an inferior judge, after the days of the charge are fering poind-elapsed, to be executed against his personal estate, or any part of on a horn-ir, or shall be under diligence by horning and caption, and shall or be imprisoned, or retire to the Abbey % or any other privileged cd, or retire to place, or fly or abscond for his personal security, or defend his the Abbey.&c. person by force; or if any debtor out of Scotland, or who cannot be imprisoned by reason of privilege, shall be under diligence by letters of horning duly denounced and registered, and shall have his or her personal estate, or any part thereof, attached by ar-reftment j it shall be lawful to the creditor or creditors at whose instance the said diligence proceeds, to apply to the court of fef-
